Strategy: Rosa: cast Shell on the entire party before Tidal Wave hits — Shell halves the ~1,500 damage to ~750, which is survivable. Then Curaga after each Tidal Wave. Rydia: Ifrit or Titan (non-water summons). Cecil: physical. Edge: Throw Shurikens. Firion: N/A (wrong game — Edge and Cecil physical). Long fight but Shell makes it manageable. Reward: Rydia learns Leviatan summon.
Adamant Armor — Don't Miss This
  • Inside the Feymarch, there is a chest containing a Rat Tail. Take it to the Mythril area (underground town of Mythril, southwest of Tomra). A dwarf there exchanges the Rat Tail for Adamant Ore.
  • Take the Adamant Ore to Kokkol's Forge (northwest underground area). He forges the ore + a Legend Sword (buy from the Feymarch shops) into the Adamant Armor — one of the best armor pieces in the game for Cecil. Return after advancing the story significantly (Kokkol takes time to forge it).
The Adamant Armor is the best armor Cecil can wear in the Lunar Subterrane. Getting the Rat Tail → Adamant Ore → Adamant Armor chain done before the Giant of Bab-il is the ideal timing. Don't miss the Rat Tail chest in the Feymarch.
7

Tower of Babel & Giant of Bab-il

▾
Tower of Babel — Fiend Rematches
  • The Tower of Babel connects the underground world back to the surface — a 7-floor tower. This is where you fight three of the four Fiends again before the Giant of Bab-il sequence.
  • Floors 1–2: Gargoyle-type enemies, Wyvern. Chests: Dry Ether, Elixir. Head toward the center stairway.
  • Floor 3 — Boss: Scarmiglione (Rematch) — Weaker than his underground version. Earth element — cast Float first to nullify his Quake. Then physical and Blizzaga.
  • Floor 4 — Boss: Cagnazzo (Rematch) — Same tactics: Shell first, then Thunder when his shell is open. He goes down faster this time with Rydia's Thundaga.
  • Floor 5 — Boss: Barbariccia (Rematch) — Kain is back — use his Jump every turn to pierce her tornado. Rosa: Curaga after Maelstrom hits.
  • Floor 6 — Boss: Rubicante (Rematch) — Same as before: Blizzaga when cloak is open. He restores your HP/MP again (out of respect) before the fight. Accept the gift. Rydia's Blizzaga hits for 4,000+ damage when his cloak is open.
  • Floor 7: Exit to the surface. The Giant of Bab-il is in sight.
Giant of Bab-il
  • A massive mechanical humanoid figure crashes onto the surface world — the Giant of Bab-il is a weapon built from ancient technology. It's destroying everything. The Dwarven tanks emerge to fight it (story cutscene).
  • Yang sacrifices himself: inside the Giant, he pushes a detonation switch that destroys the main control room — you and the party escape but Yang stays behind. He is believed dead. (He survives, in a coma — you'll find him later.)
  • FuSoYa (a Lunarian elder) descends from the moon with Golbez — who is now free from Zemus's control. Both join temporarily to fight the Giant's core.
Boss: CPU (Giant's Brain) — ~25,000 HP, with sub-components:
Aiming (~6,000 HP — increases CPU's attack power while alive)
Breath (~3,000 HP — reduces physical damage to CPU while alive)
Wave (~6,000 HP — restores CPU's HP while alive)
Strategy: Kill Aiming first (removes the attack buff — otherwise CPU uses Beam attacks that deal ~800 to all). Then Wave (stops the healing). Then destroy Breath and focus the CPU. FuSoYa and Golbez can cast Meteor — use FuSoYa's MP freely (he leaves after this battle). Golbez: Holy. Rosa: Curaga.
Before entering the Giant of Bab-il: fully equip Cecil, Kain, Rosa, Rydia, and Edge with the best gear you have. FuSoYa and Golbez join with powerful stats but leave after the CPU fight — do not waste resources equipping them. Pick up Adamant Armor from Kokkol's Forge (if you started that chain) before entering.
8

The Moon — Bahamut & Lunar Subterrane

▾
The Moon — Getting There
  • FuSoYa reveals that Zemus — a rogue Lunarian who sought to destroy humanity — is on the Moon, controlling everything from a long sleep. The Lunar Whale (a giant whale-shaped flying vessel sealed by ancient magic) rises from the ocean after Kain visits its location.
  • Inside the Lunar Whale: a full rest point (the bed fully restores HP/MP), an Ether shop, and a Hi-Potion stockroom. Use it before every major dungeon on the Moon.
On the Moon — Exploration
  • The Moon has 3 locations: Bahamut's Lair (optional), Lunar Path (connects to the Subterrane), and surface areas with stronger random encounters than anything on Earth.
  • The Lunar Path is a short multi-floor cave connecting the Moon's surface to the Lunar Subterrane. Strong enemies (Lunar Bahamuts, Metal Dragons) appear here. Use the Lunar Whale's rest before entering.
Bahamut's Lair — Optional but Essential
  • Bahamut's Lair is found on the Moon's surface. The dungeon is 3 floors with Behemoth and Dragon-type enemies. The Dragon-types resist most magic — physical attacks from Cecil and Kain, Throw from Edge.
  • Chests: Crystal Ring, Lunar equipment fragments. Pick everything up.
Boss: Bahamut — ~35,000 HP
Mechanic: Bahamut counts down 3 turns and then uses Mega Flare (deals ~9,999 to the entire party — instant wipe if you don't prepare).
Strategy Option 1 — Reflect: Rosa casts Reflect on all four party members the moment the fight starts. When Mega Flare fires, it bounces off Reflect and hits Bahamut for ~9,999. This deals massive damage to him and you take zero. Then burn him down with Rydia summons + Cecil physical.
Strategy Option 2 — Race: Use the 3-turn countdown to deal as much damage as possible. Rydia: summon Leviatan. Kain: Jump. Cecil: Excalibur. Edge: Throw ×2 Shurikens. If you deal ~15,000 in those 3 turns you'll survive the first Mega Flare with Curaga, then repeat.
Reward: Rydia learns Bahamut summon (deals 9,999 non-elemental damage to all enemies — the strongest summon in the game).
Lunar Subterrane — Final Dungeon Pre-Zeromus
  • The hardest dungeon in FF4. 8 floors of extremely tough enemies. Random encounters include Behemoths (Meteor on death), Lunar Dragons, and Mind Flayers (MP drain). Stock 20 Elixirs and 20 Dry Ethers before entering.
  • Floors B1–B4: Strong but manageable. Enemies attack in large groups. Rosa: Curaga + Shell when party HP drops. Kain: Jump. Rydia: Bahamut if needed. Edge: Throw Shurikens at large HP enemies.
  • Floors B5–B8: Brutal. Enemies here hit for 500–1,000 per attack. Keep HP above 800 at all times. Chest inventory on these floors: Crystal Sword (Cecil's best weapon), Crystal Shield, Crystal Helm, Crystal Mail (full Crystal set for Cecil and Kain — equip immediately when found). Also White Robe for Rosa, Black Robe for Rydia — these are the best endgame armor.
  • Save before floor B8. The path leads directly to Zemus and then Zeromus.
  • Zemus: FuSoYa and Golbez appear and destroy Zemus together. They unleash Holy and Meteor. Zemus dies. This seems like the end — but Zemus's hate, purified by death, becomes Zeromus. Golbez and FuSoYa cannot fight Zeromus — they're weakened. It's up to Cecil's party.
Final Boss: Zeromus — ~65,000+ HP (the embodiment of Zemus's hatred)
First step: Use the Crystal (given to you by the Heroes of Light from the surface) — it reveals Zeromus's true form. Without it, attacks do 0 damage.
Attacks: Big Bang (party-wide ~2,500 damage — fires every 3–4 turns), Flare (single target ~1,000), Meteo (random hits totaling ~3,000)
Strategy: Rosa: cast Curaga immediately after every Big Bang — the whole party will be near death and he will attack again. Rosa must never miss a healing turn. Rydia: Bahamut every turn (9,999 to Zeromus). Kain: Jump — avoid Big Bang while in the air AND deal double physical damage. Cecil: Cover to protect Rosa from Flare (Cecil takes the hit for her). Edge: Throw Shurikens (3,000–5,000 damage each).
Key survival rule: If Rosa falls, resurrect her FIRST. Without healing, Big Bang will wipe the party in 2 uses. Keep Rosa alive above all else.
Rosa's Berserk trick: Cast Berserk on Cecil and Kain early — Berserk raises attack power significantly and they'll auto-attack continuously. This frees you from managing their turns and lets you focus entirely on Rydia and Rosa.
After Zeromus: the story's emotional payoff comes from every character who survived the journey — Palom and Porom are restored from stone, Yang wakes from his coma, Cid is fine, Golbez and FuSoYa return to eternal sleep on the Moon. The ending credits cycle through every character. For a SNES game's story depth, FF4 stands apart.
✦

Guide Notes

▾

Research based on GameFAQs (Absolute Steve, Zeric guides), FF4 wiki, and community resources for the Pixel Remaster version.

Complete Walkthrough · 23 Jobs · Floating Continent to Cloud of Darkness

Final Fantasy I I I

✦ ✦ ✦
Pixel Remaster Edition

Four orphans chosen by crystals. Twenty-three jobs mastered through battle. A world balanced between light and darkness — and a final boss who cannot be defeated by the power of light alone. Final Fantasy III introduces the full job system and remains one of the series' most pure expressions of class-based strategy.

✦

Introduction & Essential Tips

▾

Final Fantasy III was never officially released outside Japan until the Nintendo DS remake in 2006. The Pixel Remaster uses the original NES version's story and content (not the DS remake's 3D version) with updated graphics, music, and QoL features. The four Warriors of Light are Luneth, Arc, Refia, and Ingus.

Core Mechanics
  • Job Points (JP): Switching jobs costs Capacity Points. You build up CP by fighting. Mastering jobs is optional but grants permanent stat bonuses.
  • Job Mastery: Each job has a mastery level (indicated by a number). At level 99 in a job, a character gets a permanent stat bonus even when in another job.
  • Specific jobs are required for certain dungeons. The game will tell you when a small body or mini-form is needed. Keep a Devout or Scholar in the party for specific puzzles.
  • The final dungeon requires high-level jobs. Do not attempt the Crystal Tower under-leveled. Recommended: at least two characters with a mastered offensive job.
  • Save at every Crystal. There is no way to save inside the Crystal Tower or Forbidden Land Eureka.
Job Tier Summary
Early game: Warrior, Red Mage, White Mage, Black Mage. Mid-game: Knight, Monk, Dragoon, Scholar. Late game: Ninja, Sage, Devout, Dark Knight, Onion Knight (secret). The Onion Knight is the weakest job until it's mastered — it becomes the strongest in the game at mastery level 99.
✦

Job System Guide

▾
Jobs by Crystal
Wind Crystal
Altar Cave (start)
Warrior, Monk, Red Mage, White Mage, Black Mage, Thief
Water Crystal
Nepto Temple area
Scholar, Geomancer, Dragoon, Viking, Dark Knight, Bard
Fire Crystal
Molten Cave
Evoker, Magus, Knight, Devout, Summoner, Sage
Earth Crystal
Crystal Tower
Ninja, Ranger, Black Belt, Onion Knight (hidden)
Recommended Late-Game Setup
  • Ninja: Dual-wield, fast, Throw shurikens. Best physical job in endgame.
  • Sage: Casts both white and black magic with equipment slots. The utility mage.
  • Devout: Best healer in the game. More spell slots than White Mage.
  • Dark Knight: Massive damage using HP — pair with a healer.
  • Onion Knight: Only viable at mastery 99. Equips everything, best stats. Long grind — skip unless you want the challenge.
☑

Missables Checklist

▾
  • MissableOnion Knight job: Obtained by sending letters via Mognet to specific NPCs. This system requires internet connectivity in some versions. In the Pixel Remaster, it's unlocked differently — check the Mognet system carefully early on.
  • MissableForbidden Land Eureka: You must enter before defeating the Cloud of Darkness. The Eureka armor/weapons are among the best in the game — do not skip.
  • OptionalLeviatan & Bahamut summons (Evoker/Summoner): Obtained in optional dungeon areas. Both are very powerful and worth getting.
  • OptionalHigh-level Shuriken (Ninja): Limited stock. Buy as many as you can afford before the final dungeon.
⚔

Equipment Reference & Boss Guide

▾
Best-in-Slot Equipment (Forbidden Land Eureka)
Ultima Weapon
Eureka · Best sword
The strongest physical weapon in FF3 — only usable by Knight and Ninja. Found in Forbidden Land Eureka. The damage bonus is enormous. Do NOT miss Eureka — the door closes permanently after defeating Cloud of Darkness.
Shuriken (×99)
Eureka shops · Ninja throw
Ninja's Throw command uses Shurikens for massive non-elemental damage bypassing defense. Buy the maximum stock from Eureka's item shops before closing the dungeon. Thrown Shurikens deal roughly 9,000–9,999 damage per throw at high levels. Stock as many as you can carry.
Crystal Equipment Set
Eureka · Best armor tier
Crystal armor, helmet, shield, and gauntlets represent the highest defense tier in the game. The full Crystal set on your Knight significantly reduces the brutal damage from Crystal Tower and Eureka enemies. Do not enter the final dungeon without at least partial Crystal gear.
Dark Scythe / Maximillian
Dark Knight weapons/armor
Dark Knight's signature weapons and armor — found in the World of Darkness dungeon. Maximillian is the best heavy armor for the Dark Knight who doesn't use the Crystal set. Dark Scythe deals HP-absorbing dark damage. Pair with a healer or the Dark Knight will burn through his own HP rapidly.
Sage's Staff / Sage's Surplice
Sage class equipment
Sage can equip both white and black magic to level 6. The Sage's Staff boosts both magic types and is the best weapon for your main mage. Sage replaces both Devout and Magus if leveled — however, Devout's level-8 white magic makes Devout strictly better as a healer.
Onion Sword / Onion Armor
Onion Knight at mastery 99
At Onion Knight job mastery level 99, all stats cap at 99 and the Onion equipment becomes usable — the strongest equipment in the game by a massive margin. The Onion Sword deals 9,999 damage reliably. This is the "true max" state that requires extreme grinding (tens of hours). Only pursue in a dedicated completion run.
Recommended Endgame Job Setups
Standard Clear Setup
Crystal Tower / Cloud of Darkness
Ninja (×2) + Sage + Devout. Ninjas throw Shurikens for 9,000+ non-elemental damage. Sage covers both black and white mid-tier magic. Devout heals at level 8 white magic (Curaga, Arise, Holy). This setup clears the final dungeon reliably at level 60+.
Dark Knight Setup
Alternative endgame
Dark Knight (×2) + Devout + Sage. Dark Knights deal massive HP at the cost of their own HP each attack. Devout must keep them healed constantly. High risk, high reward — Cloud of Darkness is the hardest content and Dark Knights can collapse if the healer falls behind. Bring lots of Elixirs.
Required: Mini (Small) Form
Specific dungeons
Several dungeons require the party to shrink using the Toad or Mini spell (later the Mini ability from appropriate jobs). Sneaking through small passages in the Floatland section requires Mini. Keep at least one Devout or Scholar in your party for status-shifting abilities when needed.
Boss Quick Reference
Land Turtle · Altar Cave
HP: ~1,500 · Opening boss
First boss. Uses physical attacks and Quake (earth AoE). Cast Thundara if available. Physical attacks are fine at this stage. He's immune to most status effects. Don't overthink it — just attack.
Medusa · Molten Cave
HP: ~2,500 · Petrify
Uses Glare (petrify gaze) which can instantly stone one party member. Equip Gold Needles (10+) before entering. Bring Golden Needles to un-petrify immediately. Use Thundaga and physical from Knights to keep pressure on.
Goldor · Goldor Manor
HP: ~4,000 · Gold-themed
Steals and uses gold-elemental attacks. Physical attackers work well. The notable mechanic: Goldor's Manor requires finding the Wheel of Time inside to unlock the boss room. Magic users cast Thundaga or Blizzaga.
Garuda · Sky fortress
HP: ~5,500 · Wind
Wind-element boss in the floating fortress area. Ground his wind attacks with Earth or Ice spells. Uses violent physical attacks and Tornado (reduces party HP to single digits). Keep HP above 500 at all times — Tornado then a follow-up can wipe the party.
Echidna · Eureka
HP: ~22,000 · Status spread
Guardian of Eureka. Uses wide-variety status spells (Quake, Death, Tornado, CurseNail). Equip equipment with status resistance. Ninja × 2 throwing Shurikens clears this in 3–4 rounds. The faster you kill her, the less status damage you take.
Ahriman · Eureka
HP: ~20,000 · Instant KO
Another Eureka guardian. Uses Flare, Death, and Eye attacks that inflict Petrify and KO. Ninja Shuriken spam and Sage Flare magic. Have Devout casting Arise constantly — party members will fall and need reviving repeatedly during this fight.
Cloud of Darkness · Final
HP: ~90,000 · Four fiends
The final boss. Has a massive HP pool and uses Flare Wave (party-wide ~1,500 damage each round). Two tentacles regenerate — kill them as they appear. Ninja × 2 Shuriken: 9,000+ × 2 = 18,000 per round. Sage: Flare for 4,000–8,000. Devout: Curaga every round. You need roughly 40,000+ damage per round to race ahead of Flare Wave. Level 60+ is the minimum; level 70+ is comfortable.
1

Ur & Altar Cave — Warriors of the Wind

▾
FF3's core mechanic — the Job System: Your four characters can freely switch jobs at any Inn. Fighting in a job earns Job Points (JP) — accumulating JP raises your Job Level, which improves stats and abilities for that job. You can switch jobs anytime but start at Job Level 1 in the new class. Plan ahead — the jobs you commit to in the mid-game form the foundation of your endgame power.
Altar Cave — Opening Dungeon
  • Luneth falls into a pit and wakes up alone inside the Altar Cave. This brief solo dungeon introduces the basics. Enemies: Goblin, Wolf. Head north and down the stairs.
  • Wind Crystal Chamber: The Wind Crystal speaks and grants the power of Jobs to Luneth and three others — his childhood friends in the village of Ur above.
Altar Cave — Full Run (after recruiting all four)
  • Starting jobs: Warrior (Luneth — frontline physical), White Mage (Arc — healing), Red Mage (Refia — versatile magic + sword), Thief (Ingus — fast, opens locked doors). This configuration covers all the bases for the early game.
  • Floor 1: Re-enter Altar Cave from Ur with all four characters. Enemies: Goblin, Goblin Guard. White Mage: Cure every fight even if not needed — raise the spell level early.
  • Floor 2: Chests: Broadsword (for Warrior), Leather Shield, 100 Gil. Continue north to the boss.
Boss: Land Turtle — ~300 HP
Weakness: Fire
Attacks: Tackle (single target physical), Harden (reduces physical damage — triggers when you try to attack normally)
Strategy: When Land Turtle hardens its shell, physical attacks become nearly useless. Red Mage and any Black Mage: cast Fire every turn. The Warrior should also use the Fire spell tome if you bought one in Ur. Do not waste turns with physical hits after it hardens. 3–4 Fire casts should be enough.
Kazus & Canaan — The Curse
  • Both towns are cursed by the Djinn's magic — all inhabitants are semi-transparent ghosts unable to interact with the world. Speak to the townspeople to learn the backstory.
  • Travel to Castle Sasune northeast of Ur. The castle is accessible and its knights are similarly cursed. Princess Sara is determined to break the curse herself — she joins temporarily as your 5th party assist character.
Castle Sasune Cavern — Djinn Dungeon
  • Floor 1–2: Undead and ghost-type enemies. Sara can cast Aero (wind damage) and has healing ability. Use Fire against undead. Chests: Mythril Sword, Mythril Shield, Potion ×3.
  • Floor 3 (Boss): The Djinn floats in the final chamber. Use a Tent before engaging.
Boss: Djinn — ~600 HP
Weakness: Ice / Wind
Attacks: Blaze (fire AoE), Leech (HP drain), Poison Gas (inflicts Poison)
Strategy: Sara automatically uses Mallet (reduces Djinn's attack power) at the start of the fight. Use Blizzard from Arc/Refia. Keep party above 150 HP — Blaze will chip everyone down. Sara's assistance reduces the difficulty significantly. Cure between rounds.
Reward: Djinn is sealed in Sara's magic ring. The curse on Kazus and Canaan lifts instantly. Sara stays at her castle.
After Djinn: upgrade equipment in Kazus (now uncursed — the shop reopens). Buy Antidotes and Hi-Potions. Next: travel to the Viking's Cove on the coast to the east. The Vikings have a ship you need.
2

Viking's Cove, Nepto Temple & Water Crystal

▾
Viking's Cove — Getting the Ship
  • The Vikings of Tokkul have a ship but won't give it freely. Their captain, Ingus's ally, eventually lends the ship if you prove your worth — or in story terms, after the Nepto Dragon is dealt with.
  • The Nepto Dragon has gone berserk — it stole the crystal eye from the Nepto Shrine and its rage is blocking sea travel. The Vikings can't leave either.
  • Getting Mini: You need the Mini spell before entering Nepto Shrine. Buy Mini tome from the Viking town's shop. Cast it on all four party members.
Nepto Shrine — Mini Dungeon
  • Critical mechanic: Cast Mini on all four characters before entering the small entrance at the base of the Nepto Shrine. In Mini form you can navigate tiny passages — in normal size you cannot enter at all.
  • While Mini: Your physical attack power is drastically reduced. Do NOT attempt to fight physically — use magic only. Keep a stock of Antidotes (many enemies here inflict Poison).
  • Floor 1 (tiny): Rat-type enemies fill the dungeon. Use Fire/Thunder magic. Navigate the small passages to the deeper levels. Chests: Mage Robe (great for mages), Potion ×4.
  • Floor 2: More rats, Mega Rats (strong for mini enemies). Continue using magic. The Giant Eye statue is visible in the background — follow the path toward it.
Boss: Giant Rat — ~780 HP
Immunity: Physical attacks (Mini party can't do meaningful damage)
Weakness: Fire
Attacks: Scratch (physical), Poison Claws (Poison on hit)
Strategy: Magic only. Fire from all four characters. If anyone gets Poisoned, Antidote immediately or they'll drop fast with each turn. 5–6 Fire casts kills it.
  • After Giant Rat: restore the Crystal Eye to the Nepto statue. The Dragon calms. Cast Mini again (or rest at the inn) to return to normal size. The Vikings release the ship.
Water Crystal — New Jobs
  • The Water Crystal is found at the bottom of the Subterranean Lake dungeon (a short dungeon before the ship area — boss is a Kraken variant). The Crystal grants: Scholar (item analysis + double-damage items), Geomancer (terrain-based free magic), Dragoon (Jump for double damage), Viking (tank, Provoke), Dark Knight (high damage, self-drains HP), Bard (support songs).
  • Recommended: Switch Luneth to Dragoon. His Jump damage will carry you through the next two sections. Keep Arc as White Mage. Keep Refia as Red Mage. Ingus: try Dark Knight (high damage but monitor HP).
Goldor's Manor — Freeing the Enterprise
  • The villain Goldor has chained the airship (Enterprise) with a magical Golden Chain. He is an incredibly wealthy man who hordes the world's gold in his mansion dungeon.
  • Manor layout: 3-floor maze filled with gold-themed traps and treasure. Golden doors, golden enemies. Enemies: Gold Knight (physical, high def), Golden Armor (heavy hitter). Use magic and Dragoon Jump.
  • Chests: Many gold-colored treasure chests throughout — most contain good items (Mythril gear, Hi-Potions, Ether). Pick up everything.
  • Boss: Goldor — Uses Thunder-based attacks, high physical defense. Have Refia cast Blizzard and Arc use Cure. Dragoon Jump from Luneth deals reliable damage. The Golden Chain breaks after his defeat — the Enterprise is yours.
After getting the Enterprise airship, the world opens up. Fly to the Town of Amur (far east) to learn about the next Crystal. Before heading to Hein's Castle, grind your party to Job Level 10+ in your current roles — Dragoon Jump becomes much stronger at higher job levels.
3

Doga, Unei & the World Below

▾
Hein's Castle — The Rotating Dungeon
  • The scholar Hein has taken over the Scholars' Village of Amur and kidnapped the village elders. He lives in a floating castle that rotates its elemental weakness — the castle itself cycles between Fire, Ice, and Thunder resistance.
  • Dungeon mechanic: Every few floors, the castle rotates. Its walls change color (red/blue/yellow) indicating which element it currently is — and NPCs inside will hint at the weakness. When the castle is red (Fire aligned), use Ice. When blue (Ice), use Thunder. When yellow (Thunder), use Fire. Hitting the wrong element does reduced damage to enemies.
  • Floors 1–3: Castle guards, Wraith-type undead, Sorcerers. Pick up chests: Hein's Wand (found after the boss), Ice Horn item (summons ice attack), Flame Sword. Navigate upward via rotating stairways.
  • Floor 4 (Boss): Hein waits here with the captured elders visible behind him.
Boss: Hein — ~3,200 HP
Mechanic: Hein cycles between absorbing Fire, Ice, and Lightning. An in-battle indicator or the environment color tells you the current weakness.
Attacks: Blizzara (ice party damage), Thunder (lightning single), Fire (fire single)
Strategy: Hit him with whichever element he's NOT aligned to. If he's absorbing Fire, use Blizzard and Thunder — vice versa. Keep cycling. Dragoon Jump from Luneth (physical — not elemental) always does normal damage regardless of rotation. Arc: Curaga every round.
Fire Crystal — New Jobs
  • The Fire Crystal is found at the bottom of Goldor's Forbidden Land (accessible after Hein) — or alternatively in the story's natural progression to the surface world. The crystal grants: Evoker (random summon magic), Magus (strongest black magic class), Knight (Cover mechanic protects allies), Devout (strongest white magic class), Summoner (controlled summoning), Sage (uses both white and black magic).
  • Critical switch: Change at least one character to Devout immediately — Devout casts Curaga more effectively than White Mage and gets higher-tier spells. Change one to Knight — the Cover ability protects weak party members (like your healer) automatically. Keep Luneth as Dragoon for now.
Doga's Grotto & Unei's Shrine
  • Doga and Unei are the last two survivors of an ancient civilization that created the Crystal Tower and sealed the World Below. They serve as guides and give you the keys to progress.
  • Doga's Grotto: A 3-floor underground cave with strong enemies. Doga gives you the Doga's Grotto Key to access the Ancients' Maze. Chests: Excalibur (found later in Eureka, not here — Doga's Grotto contains high-tier armor), Diamond Armor, Diamond Shield.
  • Unei's Shrine: Unei controls the Nautilus (a special submarine). She gives you its key, opening the World Below. Her shrine is a 2-floor dungeon with water enemies. Chests: Nautilus Shell, Diamond Helm.
  • Ancients' Maze: A sprawling 6-floor dungeon connecting the surface continent to the World Below. Enemies here are the strongest yet — bring your best Dragoon Jump and Devout healing. Chests throughout: Elixir ×3, Hi-Ether ×2, Diamond equipment.
Doga & Unei's Sacrifice
  • After descending to the World Below and confronting the Crystal Tower's sealing mechanism, Doga and Unei reveal the bitter truth: the seals on the Crystal Tower can only be broken by the death of the people who originally cast them — themselves.
  • They ask you to fight and defeat them. Both battles happen in sequence — these are not random encounters, they are scripted duels where Doga and Unei hold back to let you win. You must attack them. After both are defeated, the seals break. They die by your hands, willingly.
  • This is one of FF3's most genuinely affecting story moments. The party has been guided by these two all game — and now must kill them to proceed.
Before the Crystal Tower: switch to the recommended endgame party — Ninja × 2, Devout × 1, Sage × 1. If you've been building Ninja JP since the Earth Crystal, your Ninjas will be very powerful. Alternatively: Knight, Dragoon, Devout, Sage for a tankier approach. Stock 20 Elixirs and 99 Hi-Potions before entering the Tower.
4

Crystal Tower

▾
The Crystal Tower has no save point inside in the original version. The Pixel Remaster adds a save feature, but be cautious — if you save in a bad state between bosses, you may be stuck. Stock heavily before entry: 20 Elixirs, 99 Hi-Potions, 10 Cottages.
Crystal Tower — Floor by Floor
  • Floor 1: Entry hall. Enemies immediately ramp up — Crystal Dragon (strong physical), Medusa (Petrify gaze — equip Ribbons or Protect Rings if available). Head northwest to the staircase.
  • Floor 2: Branching paths. Take the east path first for chests: Genji Helmet, Genji Gloves (two of the best equips in the game). Then continue north.
  • Floor 3: Boss gate — Cerberus blocks the path.
Boss: Cerberus (3-headed guard dog) — ~15,000 HP
Attacks: Triple attack (hits 3 characters in one turn), Blaze (fire AoE), Haste (speeds himself)
Strategy: Devout: Curaga immediately after Triple Attack wipes your front row's HP. Ninja: Throw Fuma Shurikens for 4,000–7,000 per throw. Sage: Flare. Fast fight if your Ninjas are leveled — he dies quickly to throw damage.
  • Floors 4–5: More Crystal Dragons and Medusa. Keep Ribbon equipped on your most critical characters. Chests: Crystal Armor, Crystal Shield, Crystal Helm (the strongest armor tier).
  • Floor 6: Two boss gates in sequence — Ahriman then Echidna.
Boss: Ahriman (giant floating eye) — ~18,000 HP
Attacks: Glare (Petrify — kills a character instantly if not protected), Maelstrom (reduces all HP to single digits), Flare
Strategy: Ribbon or Protect Ring on all characters is mandatory for Glare. After Maelstrom, heal immediately before he attacks again — everyone is near death. Ninja throw + Sage Flare. Fast burn.

Boss: Echidna (serpent) — ~20,000 HP
Attacks: Earthquake (earth AoE — cast Float to nullify it), Poison, Stone Gaze, Tornado (HP reduction to single digits)
Strategy: Cast Float on all party members before the fight (or use Float spell from your Sage). This completely nullifies Earthquake — her most dangerous attack. Then burn her down with throws and Flare.
  • Floor 7 (Top — Earth Crystal): The Earth Crystal is here. Interacting with it grants the final set of jobs: Ninja (strongest physical damage class, Throw), Ranger (powerful ranged attacks), Black Belt (unarmed master, auto-counter), Onion Knight (secret class — very weak at Job Level 1 but becomes the strongest class at max Job Level 99).
  • Two Crystal Guardians block the Earth Crystal — fight them. They use Blizzaga and Flare, take physical hits, and fall quickly to Ninja throws.
After the Earth Crystal: switch ALL characters to Ninja immediately. Even at Job Level 1, Ninja's Throw command deals strong damage, and you'll be raising their JP in Eureka. The Forbidden Land Eureka is now accessible — this is where the best equipment is. Do NOT go directly to the Cloud of Darkness without clearing Eureka first.
5

Forbidden Land Eureka & Final Boss

▾
Forbidden Land Eureka — Equipment Dungeon
  • Eureka is a labyrinthine dungeon accessible from the bottom of the Crystal Tower via a hidden passage. This is where the best weapons in FF3 are found.
  • Enemies: Incredibly powerful — Ninja, Sorcerer, and Dragon-type enemies with massive HP and devastating attacks. Your own Ninjas throwing Fuma Shurikens is the most efficient way through. Run from fights you don't need.
  • Floor 1: Entry. Chests: Crystal Sword, Crystal Bow. Enemies: Ninja (ironic — fought by Ninjas), Magic Dragon. Head north and west.
  • Floor 2: Branching paths. Chests: Excalibur (holy-element sword — one of the two best swords in the game, equip on your Knight if you have one), Ragnarok (strongest non-elemental sword — equip on your best physical fighter). Getting both swords is the main reason to clear Eureka.
  • Floor 3: Chests: Onion Sword / Onion Armor (only equippable by Onion Knight — if you have one at high JP these become the strongest gear in the game), Crystal equipment pieces you may have missed. Boss gate for optional superboss Titan.
  • Save before leaving Eureka. The path from Eureka leads directly to the Cloud of Darkness fight — there is very little separation between the dungeon exit and the final boss.
Final Boss: Cloud of Darkness
  • The Cloud of Darkness is the primordial force of the Void — a being of pure darkness seeking to pull all light into oblivion. She is the true power behind the World of Darkness that threatens to consume everything.
  • Pre-battle: The four Warriors of the Dark (NPC heroes from the World Below) appear to assist — they weaken the Cloud of Darkness's Particle Beam, making the fight possible. Without their sacrifice, she would be invincible.
  • Recommended final party: Ninja × 2, Devout × 1, Sage × 1. Alternatively: Knight (Excalibur), Dragoon, Devout, Sage.
Final Boss: Cloud of Darkness — ~60,000 HP (two-phase fight)
Mechanics: She has two Tentacles of Darkness that attack each turn. The tentacles regenerate if you don't kill the Cloud fast enough. You cannot target the Cloud directly while tentacles are alive in some versions — kill them first, then focus the Cloud.
Attacks: Particle Beam (party-wide ~1,000 damage), Evil Mist (Blind + Poison on all), tentacle strikes (300–500 per tentacle per turn)
Phase 1: Kill both Tentacles immediately. Sage: Flare/Holy on a tentacle. Ninja: Throw Fuma Shuriken on the other tentacle. Devout: Curaga every single round — do not skip healing.
Phase 2 (Tentacles destroyed): Focus all fire on the Cloud herself. Ninja: Throw Fuma Shurikens (5,000–9,999 damage per throw). Sage: Flare alternating with Curaga backup. Devout: Curaga every turn. Keep everyone above 800 HP — Particle Beam hits ~1,000 to all.
Key: If you run out of Fuma Shurikens, use regular Shurikens, then hand-equip your Ninja with Ragnarok/Excalibur from their inventory and attack normally. Haste on Ninjas first turn doubles their throw frequency.
The Cloud of Darkness references the original NES/Famicom ending directly — she represents the balance mechanic of the FF3 universe: too much Light (crystals) unbalances the world, pulling Darkness to compensate. This thematic twist (the heroes using the crystals are actually causing the problem they're trying to solve) is remarkably sophisticated for 1990.
✦

Guide Notes

▾

Research based on GameFAQs (Split Infinity guide), FF3 wiki, and Pixel Remaster community documentation.

Complete Walkthrough · Action-Based Growth · Every Companion

Final Fantasy I I

✦ ✦ ✦
Pixel Remaster Edition

Final Fantasy II throws out levels entirely. Your stats grow from how you fight — use swords to raise strength, take hits to raise HP, cast magic to raise spell power. Three friends join a rebel alliance against a ruthless Empire in one of the series' darkest stories. Every character you meet has a name, a fate, and usually a tragic one.

✦

Introduction & Essential Tips

▾

Final Fantasy II is unique in the entire series: there are no traditional experience levels. Every stat grows based on what you do in battle. This makes it both more flexible and more exploitable than any other FF game. The Pixel Remaster adds auto-battle and speed toggles, but the growth system is unchanged.

Growth System Rules
  • Weapon skill: Use a weapon type repeatedly to become more accurate and powerful with it. Switching weapons resets your investment.
  • Magic power: Cast a spell repeatedly to level it up (max level 16). Higher levels = more damage/healing/duration. Each spell levels independently.
  • HP growth: The amount of damage you take in a battle (not including kills) determines how much your max HP grows. Intentionally taking hits is valid strategy.
  • MP growth: Cast magic regularly. MP grows with use.
  • Strength, Agility, Stamina, Intelligence, Spirit: Each grows based on what actions dominate your turns in a battle.
  • Never change your weapon type mid-game unless intentional — you will lose significant weapon skill investment.
Keyword System
FF2 uses a keyword dialogue system. "Learn" words from NPCs and use them in conversations to unlock new information and story progress. Always cycle through all keywords with every important NPC — missing keywords can block story progression.
✦

Stat Growth Strategy

▾
Recommended builds for the three permanent characters
Firion
Primary: Swords or Axes
Spec him into a single weapon type and Barrier/Berserk/Shell for support. He becomes the tank. High HP investment — let him take hits.
Maria
Primary: Black Magic
Level Fire, Blizzard, Thunder early. Add Flare and Ultima once obtained. Keep a bow equipped for physical turns but she's your magical powerhouse.
Guy
Primary: Axes or Bare Fists
Axes do tremendous damage with high strength. He can also communicate with animals — useful in a couple of story moments. Pure physical.
HP Grinding (optional)
The "HP trick": have party members attack each other (or hit themselves) at the start of each battle to take damage, then heal. This rapidly increases max HP. It's tedious but makes hard dungeons much safer. The Pixel Remaster's auto-battle makes this less necessary than before.
✦

Characters & Rotating Companions

▾
Firion
Permanent
Main hero. Rebels against the Empire alongside Maria and Guy after their village is destroyed.
Maria
Permanent
Firion's companion. Her brother Leon was captured. Her search for him drives much of the story.
Guy
Permanent
The strong, gentle giant. Speaks to animals. Pure physical powerhouse.
Minwu
First companion
White Mage serving the rebellion. Joins early, leaves for Mysidia. Returns in the endgame — and sacrifices himself to break the Ultima seal.
Josef
Second companion
A villager who helps in Semitt Falls. Sacrifices himself to save the party from a boulder trap — one of FF2's many gut-punch moments.
Gordon
Third companion
Cowardly prince of Kashuon who finds courage over time. Weak combatant but important story figure.
Leila
Fourth companion
A pirate captain who joins reluctantly. Fast, physical attacker with a knife. Leaves when the Dreadnought mission ends.
Ricard Highwind
Fifth companion
A Dragoon — the last of his kind. Uses Jump. Sacrifices himself to hold back the Emperor (who returns from Hell) so the party can escape.
Leon
Final companion
Maria's brother. The Dark Knight — he served the Emperor willingly after the Emperor's death elevated him to shadow ruler. Joins for the endgame.
⚔

Equipment Reference & Boss Guide

▾

In FF2 there are no traditional levels — your stats grow from use. Equipment matters because it affects base defense and evasion. Weapon skill proficiency grows separately from the weapon's innate power. The following lists endgame best-in-slot targets and key boss strategies.

Best Weapons by Type
Firion — Swords
BEST: Excalibur / Masamune
Excalibur (Holy, bonus vs undead) found in Mysidia Tower after Ultima is obtained. Masamune (best raw attack) found in Pandemonium late chests. Spear is also strong (Dragoon Spear from Deist). Invest heavily in one weapon type — switching resets weapon skill.
Maria — Bows
BEST: Yoichi Bow + Yoichi Arrow
The Yoichi Bow (best bow) and Yoichi Arrows (best arrows) are found in the Jade Passage and Pandemonium chests. Maria's primary role is Black Magic but her bow attacks deal solid physical backup damage. Keep Bow skill leveled even as magic grows.
Guy — Axes
BEST: Gigantaxe
Gigantaxe is the best axe in the game — found in Pandemonium's treasure chests. Guy is a pure physical attacker; axes maximize his Strength benefit. Equip him with the heaviest armor available to tank hits while Firion and Maria output damage.
Magic — Ultima
BEST spell · Ultima Tome
Ultima is the most powerful spell in FF2 — non-elemental, hits all enemies, scales with ALL stats simultaneously (not just Magic). Found after Minwu sacrifices himself to break the Ultima Tome seal in Mysidia. Maria should reach Ultima 8+ before Pandemonium. At level 16, Ultima is effectively unstoppable.
Stat Growth Priority Guide
HP Growth
Take damage, then heal
HP grows based on how much damage you received in a battle (not kills). To grow HP fast: at battle start, have party members attack each other briefly, then heal. Auto-battle makes this easier. Target: Firion 3,000+ HP, Maria 2,000+ HP, Guy 4,000+ HP before Pandemonium.
Magic Power
Cast every fight
Cast spells every fight — even on already-dead enemies or overhealing. Fire 16, Ice 16, Thunder 16, Cure 16, Ultima 8+ = endgame goals. Casting in every battle regardless of necessity is the only way to reach these levels naturally.
Weapon Skill
Use same weapon type always
Never switch Firion's weapon type once committed. Every swing with the same weapon type builds proficiency. Sword skill 12+ makes Firion hit multiple times per turn. Evasion grows the same way — equip a shield on Guy and let enemies hit him to raise Shield Evasion.
Stat Cap
Max all = 99
All stats cap at 99. Realistically, endgame characters typically reach: HP 3,000–6,000, MP 500–800, Strength 50–70, Intelligence 50–80, Spirit 40–60. Magic levels cap at 16 — this is the most impactful cap to reach for Maria's Ultima.
Boss Quick Reference
Borghen · Semitt Falls
HP: ~300 · First real boss
Josef's nemesis. Straightforward physical fight. Hit with swords and magic. Borghen's main danger is his relatively high attack for this point in the game — keep HP above 200. Josef has special interaction here: he blocks the boulder after this fight. One of FF2's first emotional gut-punches.
Adamantoise · Dreadnought
HP: ~1,500 · Shell
Heavy physical hitter with very high defense. Magic is the answer — Fire 5+ from Maria wrecks it. Physical attacks barely scratch the shell. This is the first fight where Magic skill investment pays off significantly.
Beelzebub · Kashuon Castle
HP: ~600 · Weak: Fire
Demon boss in the haunted castle. Weak to Fire — Maria's Fire 5+ deals double damage. He inflicts Poison which persists between fights — cure with Antidote or Esuna immediately.
Gottos · Deist Cave
HP: ~800 · Dragoon
Guards the Dragoon family's legacy in Deist Cavern. Physical attacker. Ricard Highwind accompanies you here — use his Jump ability for bonus damage while he's in the party.
Emperor · Cyclone
HP: ~2,000 · Mid-game
Uses Flare Star (party AoE, massive damage) and single-target Flare. Maria's Ultima 6+ or Fire 8+ are the damage sources. Keep everyone above 500 HP before he attacks. Ricard holds the Cyclone open so you can escape — he dies here. This fight ends Disc 1/the first half of the game.
Emperor · Pandemonium (Dark)
HP: ~3,000 · Final Boss
Resurrected from Hell in his true dark form. Starfall (party AoE ~600 dmg), Flare (single ~800 dmg), Haste, Curse (status on all). Maria: Ultima 8+ every round — this is what it was all for. Firion + Leon physical. Curaga between Starfall hits. Do NOT let any character drop below 200 HP — Flare into Starfall in the same round is a wipe.
Key Items by Location
Ultima Tome
Mysidia Tower — Minwu sacrifice
Minwu breaks the seal on the Ultima Tome at the cost of his life. This gives you access to the Ultima spell — the most powerful attack in FF2. Learn it immediately and grind it on Maria to at least level 8 before entering the Jade Passage.
Excalibur
Jade Passage / Pandemonium area
The legendary holy sword — Firion's best weapon. Found in a chest in the later Pandemonium floors. Holy element means bonus damage against all undead enemies in the dungeon, which is most of them. Equip the moment you find it.
Dragoon Spear (Wyvern Lance)
Deist Cavern
Dropped by the Wyvern boss in Deist Cavern. If Firion invests in Spear skill, the Dragoon Spear (and its Jump-compatible nature) is competitive with swords. However, if Firion's sword skill is already invested, don't switch — the skill loss isn't worth it.
Cottage
Buy everywhere · Use between floors
The most important consumable in FF2. Fully restores HP and MP for the whole party. Stock 20+ before entering the Jade Passage and Pandemonium. Use one after clearing each floor — Pandemonium is 6 floors with no guaranteed safe points.
1

Altair, Semitt Falls & Salamand

▾
How FF2's leveling works: There are no experience points. Stats increase by use: fight with swords → Sword skill rises. Cast spells → Spell level rises. Take hits → HP/Stamina rises. Block with a shield → Shield Evasion rises. Cast magic every fight even if it's overkill — that's how you level spells.
Altair — Rebel Base
  • The game opens with the party fleeing Imperial soldiers. You cannot win this fight — the Emperor's knights will knock out your whole party regardless. This is scripted. Wake up in the rebel town of Altair.
  • Speak to Princess Hilda in the white manor. She's the leader of the Wild Rose Rebellion against the Palamecian Empire. She gives you your first mission keyword: Mythril.
  • Minwu joins as your 4th companion — a White Mage of high skill. He has Cure, Aero, and Esuna. Let him heal every battle to raise his Cure level.
  • Weapon training tip: Have Firion fight unarmed (bare hands) or with a Broadsword and take hits to raise his HP. Have Guy use Axes. Have Maria use Magic every fight — even against weak enemies. This is the only way to get stronger.
Salamand → Semitt Falls Mine
  • Travel northeast to the town of Poft (airship hub) then west to Salamand. In Salamand you learn the keyword Josef — speak to Josef in the inn. He knows the mines and joins as a temporary companion.
  • Stock Potions and Antidotes before entering. Semitt Falls has Sergeant and Guard enemies — use Fire and Blizzard from Maria (even at low levels these outperform physical attacks against armored soldiers).
Semitt Falls Mine — Floor by Floor
  • Floor 1 (B1): Mine tunnels. Enemies: Guard (armored soldier, weak to magic), Sergeant (hits harder, still weak to magic). Free captive miners in cells along the walls — they provide information. Head south to the stairs.
  • Floor 2 (B2): Deeper mine. Enemies: Were-Wolf (fast, strong physical), Gremlins (status attacks). Chests: Mythril Helm, Mythril Shield. Captive rebel soldiers here — free them by defeating the guard in the room. Continue south.
  • Floor 3 (B3): The deepest level. More rebel captives. Strongarm guards patrol in pairs — use Blizzard 4+ from Maria to clear them quickly. Josef leads you to the exit on the far side.
  • Exit — Boulder Trap: As you leave, Borghen (Imperial traitor) triggers a boulder trap to seal the cave. Josef holds back the boulder with his own body so the party can escape. He is crushed saving you. His daughter Nelly is all that remains. You receive Josef's Mythril Gloves — equip them on Guy.
Josef's Mythril Gloves are the only item you get from his death. Make sure to pick them up from Nelly before leaving Salamand. You cannot get them later.
After returning to Altair with the rescued soldiers, Hilda gives you a new keyword: Kashuan. Spend time now casting magic in every random encounter — get Maria's Fire spell to level 4+ before the next dungeon. Level 4 magic deals roughly 3× the damage of level 1.
2

Kashuan Keep & the Mythril

▾
Companion: Gordon (4th slot)
  • Gordon — prince of Kashuan — joins reluctantly. He's terrified of the undead that now inhabit his family castle. His stats are low and he freezes in fear; use him as a secondary healer. Don't waste good equipment on him.
  • Getting there: Travel south from Altair across the river. Kashuan Keep is northeast of Poft. You need the Canoe (obtained later) or specific route — alternatively, learn the keyword Kashuan and Cid flies you there.
Kashuan Keep — Floor by Floor
  • Floor 1 (Ground): Entry hall of the ancestral castle. Enemies: Undead soldiers (weak to Fire and Holy magic), Ghosts (magic-heavy, use Dia). Gordon reacts fearfully at certain rooms. Head north through the main hall.
  • Floor 2: Castle upper level. Enemies: Abyss Worm (physical, high HP), more undead. Chests: Mythril Sword (upgrade for Firion), Mythril Armor (equip on Firion or Guy), Mythril Shield. Take everything — Mythril gear is the best armor tier for the next two sections.
  • Floor 3: The ritual chamber. Gordon confronts the memory of his cowardice — a brief but effective story beat. Sun Flame is found here in the fireplace/altar area. This is the key objective — it will be used to destroy the Dreadnought's engine later. Pick it up.
  • Gordon stays in the castle after the mission — he will NOT join you again immediately. He appears later in the story in Altair after the Dreadnought mission.
After Kashuan Keep, return to Altair. The Empire's Dreadnought has appeared over Poft. Princess Hilda reveals the plan: board it and destroy it using the Sun Flame. Speak to Cid in Poft to charter a ride northward — and watch out for the pirate ship.
3

The Dreadnought

▾
Companion: Leila (4th slot)
  • Cid charters the party on his ship northward. En route, Leila's pirate ship attacks. Her crew boards and demands surrender. You can choose to fight or comply — either way, after a brief standoff, Leila respects the party's strength and joins them. She's a decent fighter (Bow, Knives) and a useful party member despite the rocky intro.
Dreadnought — Zone by Zone
  • Engine Deck (Lower): Entry point via a ventilation shaft. Enemies: Imperial soldiers (weak to magic), Sergeant Elite (stronger armored variant). The lower decks are a grid of corridors — head towards the prison block first to free captives, then the engine room.
  • Prison Block: Captive citizens from towns the Empire has raided are held here. Free them from cells — each provides a hint or reward. Scott's cell is in the eastern wing: Prince Scott of Kashuan (Gordon's older brother) is dying from wounds. He gives you the Ring (a story item — bring it to Princess Hilda for a revelation later) and asks you to deliver his message. He dies in the cell. You cannot save him.
  • Engine Room: Central area of the ship. Guards here are the toughest on the ship — Sergeant Captains with high HP. Use Fire 4+ and Blizzard 4+. Plant the Sun Flame in the engine core — this sets a timer.
  • Escape: The party flees via airlock. Leila pilots the getaway. The Dreadnought crashes into the ocean — a massive victory for the rebellion.
Give Hilda the Ring after the Dreadnought mission. She reveals Scott was her betrothed — she didn't know he was captured. This is important story context and unlocks her next mission briefing. Don't miss this dialogue.
After the Dreadnought: Gordon has emerged from his shame and now helps defend Altair. Return to speak to him — he provides key information about the next objective. Leila stays in Altair as well unless she's in your active party. Next: travel to Deist.
4

Deist, Mysidia & the Wyverns

▾
Deist — Home of the Dragoons
  • Travel to Deist (island west of Poft, accessible by ship). The town is almost empty — the Empire slaughtered the Dragoon order. Ricard Highwind, the last surviving Dragoon, is there with a dying Wyvern dragon. He joins as your 4th companion.
  • Ricard's Jump ability deals double damage like a classic Dragoon. He's a strong physical fighter with decent HP. He will NOT survive to the end of the game — enjoy having him.
Deist Cavern — Floor by Floor
  • The Wyvern's egg is hidden in the Deist Cavern — the Dragoon tradition for raising new Wyverns. Ricard asks you to find it.
  • Floor 1–2: Cave enemies: Wyvern (flying, fast, physical attacks), Sea Scorpion (poison tail — keep Antidotes ready). Head deeper to the warm spring at the bottom.
  • Spring Chamber (Deepest floor): A warm underground spring — perfect for incubating the Wyvern egg. The egg is found here. Ricard places it in the warmth. This payoff comes near the game's end, when the hatched Wyvern carries the party to the final dungeon. Chests in this chamber: Protect Ring (casts Barrier on equip), Power Ring. These accessories are very valuable.
Mysidia Tower — Minwu's Sacrifice
  • The Ultima Tome is sealed at the top of the Mysidia Tower — the most powerful spell ever created, locked away to prevent misuse. Minwu volunteers to break the seal himself, knowing it will kill him. He enters alone.
  • Minwu reaches the crystal at the top. He pours his own life force into breaking the seal. He dies — but Ultima is now accessible for Maria.
  • Ultima (Ultima spell): Starts at level 1. Unlike other spells which have specific elements or targets, Ultima scales purely with its own spell level. At level 8+, it hits the entire enemy party for enormous damage with no resistance. Begin grinding it immediately — cast it in every single battle even at low level to raise it.
Minwu is permanently gone after Mysidia Tower. He was your best White Mage. Now Rosa must handle all healing — make sure your Cure spell on Maria or Firion is at least level 4 before this point, as you'll be without a dedicated healer for a while.
After Mysidia, the Emperor's Dark Sky appears over the world. His darkness (the Cyclone) devastates towns and threatens the world surface. Hilda sends you to find a way to pierce the Cyclone. Gordon reveals he knows how — a bow mounted on Wyvern-back can fire the Dragoon's Lance into the eye. Next: travel to Tropical Island for the Ultima Horn.
5

Jade Passage & Pandemonium

▾
The Cyclone — Mid-Game Dungeon
  • The Emperor's Cyclone is a moving magical tornado destroying towns. The Wyvern (hatched from the egg in Deist) can carry the party into the eye of the storm.
  • Inside the Cyclone: flying enemies (Wind Gigas, Abyss Worm variants), strong wind-based attacks. Use Blizzard and Thunder. The center of the Cyclone contains the Emperor himself — this is the midgame boss fight.
  • Boss: Emperor (First Form): Uses Flare (massive single-target damage), Starfall (party AoE). Maria with Ultima 6+ can end this fight in 2 turns. Keep Curaga ready. Firion and Ricard both deal strong physical damage. After this fight — he dies. Victory seems complete.
  • Twist: The Emperor died and was resurrected from Hell, now more powerful than ever. A second version of the Emperor, empowered by death itself, now rules Pandemonium. Ricard stays behind to buy the party time to escape the disintegrating Cyclone — Ricard Highwind sacrifices himself. He goes down fighting. He will not return.
Finding Leon
  • Leon (Maria's brother, who was captured at the very start of the game) reappears — he has been serving as the Empire's Dark Knight in the Emperor's absence. He has his own dark motivations. Once the true Emperor returns, Leon's position is meaningless. He joins the party — reluctantly — to defeat the Emperor who used him.
  • Leon is a powerful dark knight fighter — strong physical stats, uses dark swords effectively. Equip him with the best sword you have.
Jade Passage — Floor by Floor
  • A literal passage through Hell connecting the surface world to Pandemonium. 4 floors of hellish enemies.
  • Floor 1: Hellfire and lava terrain. Enemies: Astaroth (demon, strong physical + fire breath), Abaddon (dark elemental). Keep party above 300 HP — enemies here hit hard.
  • Floors 2–3: More demonic enemies with high HP and aggressive attack patterns. Thunder and Ice magic remain effective. Stock up and use Elixirs freely — you won't need them after this game ends.
  • Floor 4: Entry point into Pandemonium. Chests on this floor: Lordly Robe (powerful mage armor), Genji Gloves, Crystal Armor. Equip whatever you can. Rest here with a Cottage before entering Pandemonium.
Pandemonium — The Emperor's Hell Castle
  • A massive 6-floor castle in Hell. Enemies are the strongest in the game — they hit for 500+ and have 2,000+ HP. Ultima 8+ is your salvation.
  • Floors 1–5: Winding castle corridors with branching paths. Demonic guards, Hell-Knights, and Sorcerers patrol. Use Ultima from Maria to clear rooms. Leon's physical attacks are strong enough to keep up with magic at this stage. Save Elixirs for healing emergencies rather than MP restoration — use Cottage items between floors instead.
  • Floor 6 (Throne Room): The Emperor in his final form awaits. Use a Cottage just before the final door.
Final Boss: Emperor (Dark Form) — Resurrect HP ~8,000+
Attacks: Starfall/Starstorm (party-wide ~600 damage), Flare (single target ~800), Haste (speeds himself up), Curse (random status effects on party)
Strategy: Maria: Ultima 8+ every round — this is the fight you've been grinding for. At level 8 Ultima deals 2,000+ damage to the entire enemy group. Firion and Leon: use best swords, Haste on themselves. Curaga between Starfall hits. Do NOT let HP drop below 200 on any character — Flare into Starfall in the same round is an instant wipe condition. The fight is over in 3–4 Ultima casts if Maria is properly leveled.
Ending: The Emperor is destroyed. The rebellion wins. Leon, faced with judgment from the rebellion he helped oppress, chooses to disappear rather than accept absolution. He simply walks away. Maria calls after him — he doesn't respond. The war is over, but Ricard, Minwu, Josef, and Scott are all gone. The ending is genuinely bittersweet for a game from 1988.
✦

Guide Notes

▾

Research based on GameFAQs (Split Infinity guide), FF2 wiki, and Pixel Remaster community guides.

Complete Walkthrough · 6 Jobs · All 4 Orbs · Soul of Chaos

Final Fantasy I

✦ ✦ ✦
Pixel Remaster Edition

Where it all began. Four Warriors of Light, four darkened Orbs, one time loop to unravel. Final Fantasy I stripped to its purest form: choose your party, explore the world, restore the crystals, defeat Chaos. The Pixel Remaster adds the Soul of Chaos bonus dungeons, full orchestral music, and auto-battle. This is the best the original has ever been.

✦

Introduction & Essential Tips

▾

Final Fantasy I is deliberately minimalist — no named main characters, no complex story, just four heroes on a quest to restore the world's four Elemental Orbs. The challenge comes from resource management (limited spell uses per rest), exploration, and party building. The Pixel Remaster changes spells from "charges" to standard MP, making it significantly more accessible.

Pixel Remaster Key Changes
  • MP system replaces charges: All spells now use MP instead of the original's "spell charge" system. This is a major quality-of-life improvement.
  • Auto-battle: Available at any speed. Useful for grinding but watch your HP.
  • Soul of Chaos: Four bonus dungeons (Earthgift Shrine, Hellfire Chasm, Lifespring Grotto, Whisperwind Cove) added from the GBA version. Each contains bosses from FF3, FF4, and FF5.
  • Class Change: After obtaining the Rat Tail from Citadel of Trials and trading it, your party promotes to advanced classes. This massively increases power.
  • No permanent missables: FF1 is one of the most forgiving in the series for completionists. Everything is obtainable.
Difficulty Overview
FF1 can feel brutally hard early (limited healing, random encounters) or trivially easy (over-leveled, optimized party). The sweet spot is a balanced party and not over-grinding. Recommended: stop grinding when you can clear a dungeon — difficulty will return naturally in the next area.
✦

Jobs & Class Change Guide

▾
Starting Jobs → Promoted Classes
Warrior → Knight
Best physical tank
Can equip almost everything. After class change, gains White Magic access (levels 1–3). Excellent all-rounder. Run 2 Warriors if you want a safe, powerful front line.
Thief → Ninja
Fast attacker
Weak until class change, then becomes one of the best — gains Black Magic, high speed, good armor. Worth the early-game struggle.
Monk → Master
Physical powerhouse
Highest HP in the game. Fights barehanded — do NOT equip weapons. After class change, even stronger hits. Pure physical damage dealer.
Red Mage → Red Wizard
Balanced utility
Can use both magic schools — but is capped at mid-tier spells (no Flare, no Holy). Great early, falls behind late. Best in a 4-job mixed party.
White Mage → White Wizard
Primary healer
Essential for most parties. Cure, Regen, Protect, and Holy after class change. If you don't bring one, you will regret it in the Sea Shrine and later.
Black Mage → Black Wizard
Magic nuker
Highest magic damage. Flare and the -aga tier spells after class change. Frail — keep in the back row. Devastating in the right hands.
Recommended Party Compositions
  • Balanced (recommended for first run): Warrior, Monk, White Mage, Black Mage — covers all bases, straightforward to play.
  • Power run: Warrior × 2, Monk, Red Mage — skip dedicated magic for raw physical dominance.
  • Magic-heavy: Knight, Red Mage, White Mage, Black Mage — powerful but requires careful MP management.
  • Hard mode: Thief × 4 (become Ninja × 4 post-class change) — weak early but crushes late game.
✦

Combat & Resource Tips

▾
  • Elemental weaknesses matter. Fire enemies are weak to Blizzard/Ice. Ice enemies weak to Fire. Undead enemies take extra damage from Dia/Diara and Fire. Check enemies' element before defaulting to physical.
  • Protect (White Magic level 2) is one of the most important spells. Cast it on your front-line fighters at the start of every hard dungeon — it halves physical damage.
  • Haste (Black Magic level 4) speeds up a character's attack rate. Very effective on Warriors/Monks in long fights.
  • Run from weak enemies once you're over-leveled. The encounter rate in dungeons is high — use the flee option liberally on trash.
  • Tents, Cottages, and Cabins restore HP/MP in the field. Stock several before entering any dungeon.
  • The Inn is your best friend early game. Always sleep before entering a new dungeon even if you feel ready.
⚔

Equipment Reference — Weapons, Armor & Spells

▾
Best Weapons by Class (post–Class Change)
Knight
BEST: Excalibur / Masamune
Excalibur (Holy element, strong vs undead) from the Sunken Shrine area. Masamune (best raw attack in the game, no class restriction) from Whisperwind Cove (Soul of Chaos). Equip Excalibur for the Temple of Fiends (undead enemies everywhere). Masamune for general use.
Ninja
BEST: Masamune / Katana
Ninja can equip almost anything including Katanas and Masamune. Fast with good attack. Equip Masamune or the best Katana available. Ninja can also cast Black Magic — give them Thundaga scrolls to use in Flying Fortress.
Master (Monk)
NO weapon — bare hands only
Master fights with his fists. His bare-hand attack scales dramatically with level — do NOT equip a weapon. At high levels, Master's barehanded attack rivals the strongest weapons. Equip defense-focused gear only.
Red Wizard
BEST: Rune Blade / Falchion
Red Wizard can use some swords and light armor. Rune Blade (found in Earthgift Shrine) and Falchion are his best options. Red Wizard's main value is his dual magic access — keep MP topped off via equipment that boosts MP or with Cottages.
White Wizard
BEST: Healing Staff / Thor Hammer
Healing Staff (attack to heal ~80 HP, very useful) and Thor Hammer (casts Thundara when used as item in battle) give White Wizard utility attacks. Main job is healing — prioritize armor/magic equipment over weapons. Equip Ribbon for all-status immunity.
Black Wizard
BEST: no significant weapons
Black Wizard is the weakest physical attacker. Keep him in the back row. His value is entirely from Flare (non-elemental nuke), Thundaga, Blizzaga, and Firaga. Focus on boosting his Int stat with equipment. Equip Robe gear for MP/defense.
Best Armor (post–Class Change)
Genji Armor
Flying Fortress · Floor 4 chest
The best heavy armor available in the main game for Knight/Ninja. +68 Defense. Found in a chest on Flying Fortress Floor 4 — collect before fighting Tiamat. The Genji set (Armor + Helmet) is the gold standard for physical fighters.
Genji Helmet
Flying Fortress · Floor 4 chest
Best helmet for physical classes in the main game. +20 Defense, +10 Agility. Found alongside the Genji Armor chest in Flying Fortress. Equip both on your Knight or Ninja before the final dungeon.
Ribbon
Soul of Chaos: Whisperwind Cove
Prevents ALL status effects — the best accessory in the game. Found in Whisperwind Cove (the hardest Soul of Chaos dungeon, requires level 50). Equip on your White Wizard to prevent her from being status-locked during Chaos's fight.
Crystal Armor / Crystal Helm
Soul of Chaos rewards
The strongest armor tier in the Pixel Remaster — found only in the deepest Soul of Chaos dungeons (Whisperwind Cove). Crystal Armor surpasses Genji Armor in defense. The Crystal set is the true best-in-slot if you clear the bonus dungeons.
White Robe
White Wizard only
Best robe for White Wizard — significantly boosts Spirit stat (affects healing power) and provides decent defense. Found in late-game dungeons. Equip alongside Ribbon for a White Wizard who can't be status'd and heals for maximum HP.
Black Robe
Black Wizard only
Boosts Intelligence (affects magic damage) for Black Wizard. Best mage robe in the game. Found in late-game dungeons. The Int boost meaningfully increases Flare and Thundaga damage — prioritize equipping this over defensive gear.
Full Spell List — All 8 Levels (White & Black)
White Magic L1–4
Early game spells
L1: Cure, Dia (undead damage), Protect (physical halved), Fog (blind). L2: Cure 2, Silence, Blind, Mini. L3: Cura, Diara, NulShock, NulFrost. L4: Heal (party Cure), Diaga, NulBlaze, NulDeath. Priority buys: Cure (L1), Protect (L1), Heal (L4).
White Magic L5–8
Late game spells
L5: Life (Raise), Curaga, Esuna, Odin (instant KO). L6: Curaja (best heal), Life 2 (full revive), Protera (party Protect), Holy (light damage). L7: Healara, Arise (revive full HP), NulAll, Quake. L8: Meteo (AoE damage), Holy 2/Full-Life, Wall (reflect). Priority: Curaja (L6), Arise (L7), Holy (L6).
Black Magic L1–4
Early game spells
L1: Fire, Blizzard, Thunder, Poisona. L2: Fira, Blizzara, Thundara, Sleep. L3: Firaga (buy in Elfheim), Blizzaga, Thundaga, Slow. L4: Confuse, Stop, Saber (Attack Up), Haste. Priority buys: Fire/Blizzard/Thunder (L1), all L3 spells, Haste (L4).
Black Magic L5–8
Late game spells
L5: Death (instant KO), Osmose (MP drain), Temper (Str up), Drain. L6: Flare (massive non-elemental — buy in Gaia or Onrac), Reaper, Stun, Warp (escape dungeon). L7: Flood, Break, Quartr (reduce HP by 3/4), Venom. L8: Flare 2/Nuke (strongest attack), Flare 2, Blind 2, Stop 2. Priority: Haste (L4), Temper (L5), Flare (L6).
Boss Quick Reference
Garland · Chaos Shrine
HP: 106 · No weakness
Tutorial boss. Physical attacks only. He attacks once per round at this stage. Simply attack until he falls. No strategy required beyond basic healing if needed.
Astos · Western Keep
HP: 168 · No weakness
Uses Rub (instant KO on one character) and Petrify. Keep Phoenix Downs and Golden Needles ready. Hit with physical attacks and Firaga if available. Fast fight — burst him down before he gets off too many status attacks.
Vampire · Marsh Cave
HP: 156 · Weak: Fire/Dia
Undead — Firaga and Diaga deal bonus damage. He can inflict Darkness. Heal status immediately. Straightforward fight once you use element advantage.
Lich · Earth Cave
HP: 400 · Weak: Fire/Holy
First Elemental Fiend. Undead — Dia and Fire spells do extra damage. Opens with Quake (party damage). Equip NulShock/NulBlaze if available. Burst him down with Firaga and physical attacks. White Mage: spam Diara.
Marilith · Gurgu Volcano
HP: 660 · Weak: Ice
Fire Fiend. All fire-element attacks heal her — use Ice only. Blizzaga from Black Wizard. She attacks multiple times per round with her swords — party must be at high HP. Cast Protect early.
Kraken · Sunken Shrine
HP: 800 · Weak: Lightning
Water Fiend. Thundaga wrecks him. He uses Ink (Blind on party) — cure immediately. Multiple attacks per round. Equip NulFrost/NulShock. Thundaga from Black Wizard + physical from Knight/Ninja = fast clear.
Tiamat · Flying Fortress
HP: 2,000 · Weak: Ice
Wind Fiend — the hardest of the four. Blaze hits the whole party for 200–300 each round. Party must stay above 400 HP at all times. Blizzaga from Black Wizard every turn. Haste Knight early. Cast Protect before the fight. The Megalixir from Flying Fortress Floor 3 is for emergencies here.
Chaos · Temple of Fiends
HP: 20,000 · No weakness
The final boss. 20,000 HP. Uses Curaja (heals himself for 9,999 — the biggest threat). Speed is everything — apply Haste + Temper on physical attackers. Flare from Black Wizard (non-elemental — nothing is resisted). Keep White Wizard casting Curaja every round. Must outdamage his Curaja healing to win.
1

Cornelia & Chaos Shrine — Wind Orb

▾
Job Selection — Your Most Important Decision
  • You choose four jobs from six available at game start. These are permanent until Class Change at Bahamut's Cave — roughly 60% through the game. Choose carefully based on difficulty level:
Recommended parties:
Balanced (normal): Warrior, Monk, White Mage, Black Mage — covers offense, tanking, healing, and magic damage
Physical (hard): Warrior × 2, Monk, Red Mage — powerful early but MP-limited throughout
Mage-heavy (hard but rewarding): Warrior, White Mage, Black Mage, Red Mage — excellent spell power but squishy
Advanced run: Warrior, Red Mage, Red Mage, White Mage — Red Mages handle both roles, good versatility

Thief is not recommended for normal play — he's very weak until Class Change (becomes Ninja). Red Mage is versatile (can use swords + magic) but falls behind specialists at later levels.
Cornelia — Town Setup
  • Weapons shop: Buy a Sword for your Warrior, a Nunchaku for Monk (or leave him unarmed — Monk's bare-hand damage grows very fast), and any weapon your Red Mage can use.
  • Armor shop: Buy Leather Armor for the Warrior, Cap for the White/Black Mage. Don't buy expensive armor — you'll replace it in Elfheim soon.
  • Magic shop: Buy Cure for the White Mage (critically important), Fire for the Black Mage. If you have a Red Mage, buy Fire for them too. These two spells will carry you through the entire early game.
  • Speak to King Cornelia. His daughter Princess Sarah was kidnapped by Garland — once his greatest knight, now gone mad at the Chaos Shrine to the north.
Chaos Shrine (Prologue) — Floor by Floor
  • Floor 1: Simple corridors. Enemies: Goblin (basic), Wolf (slightly tougher). The first battles — use them to level up once or twice before going deeper. Head north to the stairs.
  • Floor 2: Wider corridors. More Goblins and Wolves. Chests: Potion ×2. Continue north-northeast. Enemies don't hit very hard at this stage — conserve MP by using physical attacks.
  • Floor 3: Chests: Antidote, 200 Gil. Stronger Goblin variants appear. Keep your party above 50 HP. Stairs to the boss room.
  • Floor 4 (Garland's Chamber): Single room with Princess Sarah and Garland in the center.
Boss: Garland — ~450 HP (Level 1 difficulty)
No weakness or elemental resistance
Attacks: Sword strike (~40–60 damage), occasionally attacks twice
Strategy: At level 1–2, Garland hits for more than your max HP if you're a mage. Put mages in the back row. Warrior and Monk attack every turn. White Mage: Cure whenever anyone drops below 30% HP. Black Mage: Fire spell (deals ~50 damage — not huge but efficient). 5–8 rounds to win.
  • After Garland: Princess Sarah is freed. She gives you the Lute (a story item used at the very end of the game). Return to Cornelia.
  • King's Reward: King Cornelia builds the Bridge south of the city — connecting to the rest of the world. The main adventure begins. Cross the bridge and head south.
After the bridge: the southern marsh is dangerous (Ogres, Lizards with high HP) — do not fight them at level 1. Stay on the main path toward Pravoca (east along the coast) and Elfheim. Grind in the grass fields if you're below level 5.
2

Elfheim, Dwarven Cavern & Canal

▾
Town Circuit — Elfheim & Matoya's Cave
  • Cross the bridge south. The main road leads east through Pravoca (port town) and continues south. Pravoca has a decent equipment shop — buy Rapier for Red Mage, better shields if available.
  • Elfheim (southeast): The Elven Prince is asleep in the castle — cursed by someone. The Elves' magic shops here are valuable: buy Thunder (Black Mage), Blizzard, and White Magic spells like Protect.
  • Matoya's Cave (north of Elfheim, accessible by foot): The witch Matoya lost her Crystal Eye — stolen by a goblin. Without it, she can't brew a Jolt Tonic to wake the Elven Prince. Note the location — you'll return here after getting the Mystic Key.
  • Why the prince matters: Waking the Elven Prince gets you the Mystic Key — the key that opens all locked treasure rooms across the world.
Northwest Castle — Astos and the Mystic Key
  • Travel northwest from Elfheim (long overland route, or sail if you have a ship). The Northwest Castle has the Crown in its highest room — this is what the cursed king of the castle was searching for before he went mad.
  • Chests in Northwest Castle: Crown (key item), Mythril Gloves, Silver Sword, Hi-Potion ×3. Pick up the Crown — then be ready for a fight.
  • Travel to the Dwarven Cavern (east of Elfheim). At the cave's deepest point, an old king sits. Present the Crown — it's a trap. The "old king" is Astos, the Dark Elf villain in disguise. He attacks immediately.
Boss: Astos (Dark Elf) — ~1,000 HP, Level ~8
Weakness: Light/Holy (Dia spell)
Attacks: Rub (Death magic — instant KO, 30% chance), Blind (inflicts Darkness status on a target), physical hits
Strategy: Astos's Rub spell can instantly kill a character at random — this makes the fight dangerous even for prepared parties. Level to at least 8–10 before attempting. White Mage: Dia (Holy damage) + Cure when someone is KO'd. Black Mage: Fire or Thunder every turn. Warriors: physical. Bring 5+ Phoenix Downs — someone will likely die to Rub. Re-raise them fast.
Rewards: Crystal Eye (return to Matoya for Jolt Tonic) + Mystic Key (opens all locked rooms).
Mystic Key — Open Everything Now
  • With the Mystic Key, return to Cornelia Castle and open the locked room in the basement: Mythril Sword, Mythril Shield, Mythril Helm, 300 Gil. Equip the Mythril Sword on your Warrior immediately.
  • Return to Elfheim Castle and open the locked room: Copper Gauntlets, Heal Potion, Soft. Minor items but worth collecting.
  • Return to Matoya's Cave with the Crystal Eye. She brews the Jolt Tonic. Take it to the Elven Prince in Elfheim Castle → he wakes and gives you the Mystic Key back (it's already consumed) — actually he gives you something that tells you the next destination. The Canal gate to Melmond is now accessible.
  • Open the Canal Lock (east of Pravoca): reveals a ship in the harbor. You now have sea travel — you can sail to Melmond and the Earth Cave.
Level recommendation before Earth Cave: 10–12 minimum. The Earth Cave's floor B3 onward has enemies that hit for 80–120 per attack. Buy Life (Arise/Phoenix) tome for your White Mage if available in Elfheim — resurrection magic is critical from here on.
3

Melmond & Earth Cave — Earth Orb

▾
  • Melmond is decaying — the earth is dying around it. The Earth Crystal has been darkened by an undead vampire lord named Astos. Talk to Dr. Unne in Melmond (he's the key to the Lufenian language later) and buy the best equipment available at the shop.
Earth Cave — Floor by Floor
  • Floor B1: Standard caves with Zombie and Ghoul encounters (both inflict Paralyze — bring Antidotes or have Esuna). 3 chests: Potion, Antidote, Tent. Take the south stairs down.
  • Floor B2: More open layout. Watch for Cockatrice enemies — they inflict Stone status (carry Gold Needles). 2 chests: Hi-Potion, Leather Shield. South passage leads down.
  • Floor B3: Difficult enemies start here. Pisco Demon and Pyramid enemies. 3 chests: Antidote, Gold Needle, Tent. Navigate the two-branch corridor — take the left branch for the stairs to B4.
  • Floor B4: Vampire's lair. Only one enemy here — the Vampire boss. Treasure room has: Falchion, Cottage, Mythril Vest. Boss: Vampire — Weak to Holy (Dia spell) and Fire. One Diara from your White Mage = ~800 damage. He casts Rub (Death) — act fast. Defeat to get the Star Ruby.
    — After Vampire: take the Star Ruby and EXIT the Earth Cave. Go back to the overworld.
  • Giant's Cave: North of the Earth Cave entrance. Inside, a giant is sleeping, blocking the passage to Crescent Lake. Give him the Star Ruby — he wakes, moves aside, and the path opens.
  • Return to Earth Cave B5 (via the newly opened path from Giant's Cave): This section has the strongest enemies in the current game progression. Air Elementals and Piscodaemons.
  • Floor B5: Dark, maze-like. 4 chests: Cottage, Healing Helm, Gold Bracelet, Vorpal Sword. Follow the south wall to the stairs.
    — Boss: Lich (Earth Fiend) — The boss of the Earth Cave. Undead and extremely powerful. HP ~2,000.
    — Use Diara (White Magic level 3) — deals 600–800 damage per cast to undead. Your White Mage should spam it exclusively.
    — Lich uses Blizzaga, Quake, and Stun. Keep everyone above 200 HP. One round of Diara spam from multiple casters can win this.
    — After victory: the Earth Crystal is restored. Proceed to Crescent Lake.
  • Save Point: There is no in-dungeon save point in FF1 (Pixel Remaster uses a more traditional camp-based system). Use a Tent or Cottage before entering B5.
  • Exit: After Lich, use a Teleport scroll or walk back up through B5→B4→B3→B2→B1→surface. Teleport scrolls save significant time.
Level to 15–18 before attempting Earth Cave. The random encounters on floor 5 will wipe an unprepared party. Bring Cottages for mid-dungeon rest.
4

Crescent Lake, Gurgu Volcano & Fire Orb

▾
Crescent Lake — Town
  • The 12 Sages of Crescent Lake form a circle east of town. Walk through the ring to receive the Canoe — required to navigate rivers and reach Gurgu Volcano and the Ice Cave.
  • Shop priorities: Buy Blizzara (Ice2) and Blizzaga (Ice3) for your Black Mage/Red Mage if you haven't yet. Upgrade any armor you can afford. Stock 10+ Cottages and at least 15 Antidotes.
  • Level recommendation before Gurgu Volcano: Level 19–22. Enemies inside hit very hard — if you're below 15, grind on the world map outside Crescent Lake first.
Gurgu Volcano — Floor by Floor
  • Floor 1 (B1): Lava corridors. Enemies: Fire Lizard (absorbs fire — do not use Fire spells), Agama (fire element). These enemies are immune or absorb Fire — only use Ice or physical attacks. Head south along the corridor to the stairs.
  • Floor 2 (B2): More winding lava paths. Chests: Ice Shield (grab it — reduces your tank's fire damage taken), 2,000 Gil. Enemies: Fire Gigas appear here — they hit for 150+ per attack. Keep your mages' HP above 200 at all times. Exit is southwest.
  • Floor 3 (B3): Branching corridors. Chests: Falchon (decent sword for Warriors), Cottage (use it now or save for B4). Staircase continues south. Watch for Fire Gigas packs — they can wipe an unprepared party in two rounds.
  • Floor 4 (B4): Pre-boss floor. Chests: Flame Mail (reduces fire damage by 14 — equip on your frontliner immediately), Flame Sword (fire-elemental weapon — do NOT use it here since all enemies absorb fire; save it for undead in later dungeons). Use a Cottage on this floor before proceeding.
  • Floor 5 (Boss): Single long corridor leads directly to Marilith. No save point — use the Cottage from B4 in the corridor before the boss door.
Boss: Marilith (Fire Fiend) — ~2,000 HP
Weakness: Ice (Blizzara/Blizzaga)
Attacks: Up to 6 physical strikes per round (distributed across party), Fire2 (fire damage to one), FireBlast (party AoE fire)
Strategy: Open with Haste on your Knight/Warrior. Cast Protect on your White Mage if available. Black Mage/Red Mage: Blizzaga every round — at ~500 MP of damage per cast she dies in 3–4 casts. White Mage: Curaga spam to keep everyone above 200 HP. If she uses FireBlast when your party is low, heal immediately before attacking.
Reward: Fire Orb lit. Teleport scroll or stairs back to B1.
After Marilith, use the Teleport scroll (or Warp spell) to exit instantly. Save at Crescent Lake before attempting the Ice Cave.
5

Ice Cave, Citadel of Trials & Class Change

▾
Ice Cave — Floor by Floor
  • Canoe required to reach Ice Cave via river northwest of Crescent Lake. The cave sits in the northern snowfields.
